The stripping of MoS2 layers occurring in charge/discharge cycling contributes to the enhanced kinetics and low energy barrier for the intercalation of Na+ ions.  The electrochem. reaction is mainly controlled by the capacitive process, which facilitates the high-rate capability.  Therefore, MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayers hold promise for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp0lywDrXEibbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linR0pVpOmlxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXhvFShtL3P&amp;md5=218e207e71a96b8802293b3796174e5a</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms5033"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wen, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">He, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Han, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Matsuda, I.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ishii, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cumings, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Expanded Graphite as Superior Anode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Expanded graphite as superior anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wen, Yang; He, Kai; Zhu, Yujie; Han, Fudong; Xu, Yunhua; Matsuda, Isamu; Ishii, Yoshitaka; Cumings, John; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4033</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">NCAOBW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2041-1723</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Nature Publishing Group</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Graphite, as the most common anode for com. Li-ion batteries, has been reported to have a very low capacity when used as a Na-ion battery anode.  It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode.  Prepd. through a process of oxidn. and partial redn. on graphite, expanded graphite has an enlarged interlayer lattice distance of 4.3 Å yet retains an analogous long-range-ordered layered structure to graphite.  In situ transmission electron microscopy has demonstrated that the Na-ion can be reversibly inserted into and extd. from expanded graphite.  Galvanostatic studies show that expanded graphite can deliver a high reversible capacity of 284 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 20 mA g-1, maintain a capacity of 184 mAh g-1 at 100 mA g-1, and retain 73.92% of its capacity after 2,000 cycles.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrFEZ8wJYk1irVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linR0pVpOmlxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2MXksVeqs7g%253D&amp;md5=e4bc2edac8d22121e7986e165b7df007</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref12"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">12</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit12" data-doi="10.1021/nn502045y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lotfabad, E. P.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hazelton, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mitlin, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Density Sodium and Lithium Ion Battery Anodes from Banana Peels</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2014</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>8</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">7115</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">7129</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

                        cas_cit12R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">12</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Density Sodium and Lithium Ion Battery Anodes from Banana Peels</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lotfabad, Elmira Memarzadeh; Ding, Jia; Cui, Kai; Kohandehghan, Alireza; Kalisvaart, W. Peter; Hazelton, Michael; Mitlin, David</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">8</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">7</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">7115-7129</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Banana peel pseudographite (BPPG) offers superb dual functionality for Na ion battery (NIB) and Li ion battery (LIB) anodes.  The materials possess low surface areas (19-217 m2 g-1) and a relatively high electrode packing d. (0.75 g cm-3vs. ∼1 g cm-3 for graphite).  Tested against Na, BPPG delivers a gravimetric (and volumetric) capacity of 355 mA-h g-1 (by active material ∼700 mA-h cm-3, by electrode vol. ∼270 mA-h cm-3) after 10 cycles at 50 mA g-1.  A nearly flat ∼200 mA-h g-1 plateau that is &lt;0.1 V and a minimal charge/discharge voltage hysteresis make BPPG a direct electrochem. analog to graphite but with Na.  A charge capacity of 221 mA-h g-1 at 500 mA g-1 is degraded by 7% after 600 cycles, while a capacity of 336 mA-h g-1 at 100 mA g-1 is degraded by 11% after 300 cycles, in both cases with ∼100% cycling Coulombic efficiency.  For LIB applications BPPG offers a gravimetric (volumetric) capacity of 1090 mA-h g-1 (by material ∼2200 mA-h cm-3, by electrode ∼900 mA-h cm-3) at 50 mA g-1.  The reason that BPPG works so well for both NIBs and LIBs is that it uniquely contains 3 essential features: (a) dilated intergraphene spacing for Na intercalation at low voltages; (b) highly accessible near-surface nanopores for Li metal filling at low voltages; and (c) substantial defect content in the graphene planes for Li adsorption at higher voltages.  The &lt;0.1 V charge storage mechanism is fundamentally different for Na vs. for Li.  A combination of XRD and XPS demonstrates highly reversible Na intercalation rather than metal underpotential deposition.  By contrast, the same anal. proves metallic Li in the pores, with intercalation being much less pronounced.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpvndZF6mFnK7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linR0pVpOmlxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXpt1Krt70%253D&amp;md5=1ad531caaafd48d9545b9c814029eada</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref13"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref13'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">13</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit13" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201703772"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nayak, P.                         cas_cit13R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">13</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">From Lithium-Ion to Sodium-Ion Batteries: Advantages, Challenges, and Surprises</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Nayak, Prasant Kumar; Yang, Liangtao; Brehm, Wolfgang; Adelhelm, Philipp</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Mobile and stationary energy storage by rechargeable batteries is a topic of broad societal and economical relevance.  Lithium-ion battery (LIB) technol. is at the forefront of the development, but a massively growing market will likely put severe pressure on resources and supply chains.  Recently, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have been reconsidered with the aim of providing a lower-cost alternative that is less susceptible to resource and supply risks.  On paper, the replacement of lithium by sodium in a battery seems straightforward at first, but unpredictable surprises are often found in practice.  What happens when replacing lithium by sodium in electrode reactions.  This review provides a state-of-the art overview on the redox behavior of materials when used as electrodes in lithium-ion and sodium-ion batteries, resp.  Advantages and challenges related to the use of sodium instead of lithium are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrGeYJemvxIpbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0linR0pVpOmlxw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhvVKmurvE&amp;md5=4342a80be51730e08dc9faec2f79fb63</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref14"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref14'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">14</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit14" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201402402"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Castillo-Martínez, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Carretero-González, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Armand, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Polymeric Schiff Bases as Low-Voltage Redox Centers for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.                         cas_cit14R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">14</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Polymeric Schiff Bases as Low-Voltage Redox Centers for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Castillo-Martinez, Elizabeth; Carretero-Gonzalez, Javier; Armand, Michel</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The redox entity comprising two Schiff base groups attached to a Ph ring (of structure [-N=CH-Ar-CH=N-]) is reported to be active for sodium-ion storage (Ar = arom. group).  Electroactive polymeric Schiff bases were produced by reaction between non-conjugated aliph. or conjugated arom. diamine block with terephthalaldehyde unit.  Cryst. polymeric Schiff bases are able to electrochem. store more than one sodium atom per azomethine group at potentials between 0 and 1.5 V vs. Na+/Na.  The redox potential can be tuned through conjugation of the polymeric chain and by electron injection from donor substituents in the arom. rings.  Reversible capacities of up to 350 mA h g-1 are achieved when the carbon mixt. is optimized with Ketjen Black.  Interestingly, the "reverse" configuration (of structure [-CH=N-Ar-N=CH-]) is not electrochem. active, though isoelectronic.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrfY8JYZw4ZirVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg1bdBtYnKMBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2cXmslakur4%253D&amp;md5=53412644537ae0ee4c6334a00b670423</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref15'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201601792"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Advanced Organic Electrode Materials for Rechargeable Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Opportunities and challenges for organic electrodes in electrochemical energy storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Poizot, Philippe; Gaubicher, Joel; Renault, Steven; Dubois, Lionel; Liang, Yanliang; Yao, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemical Reviews (Washington, DC, United States)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  As the world moves toward electromobility and a concomitant decarbonization of its elec. supply, modern society is also entering a so-called fourth industrial revolution marked by a boom of electronic devices and digital technologies.  Consequently, battery demand has exploded along with the need for ores and metals to fabricate them.  Starting from such a crit. anal. and integrating robust structural data, this review aims at pointing out there is room to promote org.-based electrochem. energy storage.  Combined with recycling solns., redox-active org. species could decrease the pressure on inorg. compds. and offer valid options in terms of environmental footprint and possible disruptive chemistries to meet the energy storage needs of both today and tomorrow.  We review state-of-the-art developments in org. batteries, current challenges, and prospects, and we discuss the fundamental principles that govern the reversible chem. of org. structures.  We provide a comprehensive overview of all reported cell configurations that involve electroactive org. compds. working either in the solid state or in soln. for aq. or nonaq. electrolytes.  These configurations include alkali (Li/Na/K) and multivalent (Mg, Zn)-based electrolytes for conventional "sealed" batteries and redox-flow systems.  We also highlight the most promising systems based on such various chemistries relying on appropriate metrics such as operation voltage, specific capacity, specific energy, or cycle life to assess the performances of electrodes.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqXsrWSggozYrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg1bdBtYnKMBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXltlylsrw%253D&amp;md5=db762ca67ab50864a95013520ba83a3e</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1002/anie.201910916"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Pollard, T.                         cas_cit17R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">17</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Pyrazine-Based Polymer for Fast-Charge Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Mao, Minglei; Luo, Chao; Pollard, Travis P.; Hou, Singyuk; Gao, Tao; Fan, Xiulin; Cui, Chunyu; Yue, Jinming; Tong, Yuxin; Yang, Gaojing; Deng, Tao; Zhang, Ming; Ma, Jianmin; Suo, Liumin; Borodin, Oleg; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The lack of high-power and stable cathodes prohibits the development of rechargeable metal (Na, Mg, Al) batteries.  Herein, poly(hexaazatrinaphthalene) (PHATN), an environmentally benign, abundant and sustainable polymer, is employed as a universal cathode material for these batteries.  In Na-ion batteries (NIBs), PHATN delivers a reversible capacity of 220 mAh g-1 at 50 mA g-1, corresponding to the energy d. of 440 Wh kg-1, and still retains 100 mAh g-1 at 10 Ag-1 after 50 000 cycles, which is among the best performances in NIBs.  Such an exceptional performance is also obsd. in more challenging Mg and Al batteries.  PHATN retains reversible capacities of 110 mAh g-1 after 200 cycles in Mg batteries and 92 mAh g-1 after 100 cycles in Al batteries.  DFT calcns., XPS, Raman, and FTIR show that the electron-deficient pyrazine sites in PHATN are the redox centers to reversibly react with metal ions.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGplbkOWQcbDL7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg1bdBtYnKMBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXitValurjF&amp;md5=182b996cbe68c4a61e9b965b9a33e2ab</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref18"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref18'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">18</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit18" data-doi="10.1038/ncomms2481"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sakaushi, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hosono, E.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nickerl, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gemming, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kaskel, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Eckert, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Aromatic Porous-Honeycomb Electrodes for a Sodium-Organic Energy Storage Device</span>. <i>Nat.                         cas_cit18R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">18</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Aromatic porous-honeycomb electrodes for a sodium-organic energy storage device</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Sakaushi Ken; Hosono Eiji; Nickerl Georg; Gemming Thomas; Zhou Haoshen; Kaskel Stefan; Eckert Jurgen</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature communications</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">4</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">1485</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Rechargeable batteries using organic electrodes and sodium as a charge carrier can be high-performance, affordable energy storage devices due to the abundance of both sodium and organic materials.  However, only few organic materials have been found to be active in sodium battery systems.  Here we report a high-performance sodium-based energy storage device using a bipolar porous organic electrode constituted of aromatic rings in a porous-honeycomb structure.  Unlike typical organic electrodes in sodium battery systems, the bipolar porous organic electrode has a high specific power of 10 kW kg(-1), specific energy of 500 Wh kg(-1), and over 7,000 cycle life retaining 80% of its initial capacity in half-cells.  The use of bipolar porous organic electrode in a sodium-organic energy storage device would significantly enhance cost-effectiveness, and reduce the dependency on limited natural resources.  The present findings suggest that bipolar porous organic electrode provides a new material platform for the development of a rechargeable energy storage technology.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcRIZQvO3WT9PGZyxfu64m4ffW6udTcc2eZVII6HIvmYO7ntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A280%3ADC%252BC3sznslKguw%253D%253D&amp;md5=6fceaa517717e297e11ff4436554983b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref19"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref19'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">19</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit19" data-doi="10.1073/pnas.1717892115"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Borodin, O.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gaskell, K.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Azo compounds as a family of organic electrode materials for alkali-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Luo, Chao; Borodin, Oleg; Ji, Xiao; Hou, Singyuk; Gaskell, Karen J.; Fan, Xiulin; Chen, Ji; Deng, Tao; Wang, Ruixing; Jiang, Jianjun; Wang, Chunsheng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States of America</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">115</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2004-2009</span>CODEN:

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">National Academy of Sciences</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. compds. are desirable for sustainable Li-ion batteries (LIBs), but the poor cycle stability and low power d. limit their large-scale application.  Here we report a family of org. compds. contg. azo group (N=N) for reversible lithiation/delithiation.  Azobenzene-4,4'-dicarboxylic acid lithium salt (ADALS) with an azo group in the center of the conjugated structure is used as a model azo compd. to investigate the electrochem. behaviors and reaction mechanism of azo compds.  In LIBs, ADALS can provide a capacity of 190 mAh g-1 at 0.5 C (corresponding to c.d. of 95 mA g-1) and still retain 90%, 71%, and 56% of the capacity when the c.d. is increased to 2 C, 10 C, and 20 C, resp.  Moreover, ADALS retains 89% of initial capacity after 5,000 cycles at 20 C with a slow capacity decay rate of 0.0023% per cycle, representing one of the best performances in all org. compds.  Superior electrochem. behavior of ADALS is also obsd. in Na-ion batteries, demonstrating that azo compds. are universal electrode materials for alkali-ion batteries.  The highly reversible redox chem. of azo compds. to alkali ions was confirmed by d.-functional theory (DFT) calcns.  It provides opportunities for developing sustainable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoTFeVm6HRVbLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg1bdBtYnKMBA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitVamsr7N&amp;md5=5a61f204ec55f1c020ffc668244f973c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201713417"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Luo, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, G.-L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ji, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hou, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jiang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ren, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Amine, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, C.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Reversible Redox Chemistry of Azo Compounds for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Angew.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. electrode materials have shown great potential for metal-ion batteries because of their high theor. capacity, flexible structure designability, and environmental friendliness.  However, their electrochem. performance still needs to be further enhanced, which mainly depends on the mol. structures, electrode fabrication, electrolyte, and separators.  In this review, we present the working principles and fundamental properties of different types of org. electrode materials, including conductive polymers, organosulfur compds., org. radicals, carbonyl compds., and other emerging materials.  We then focus on the strategies toward enhancing the electrochem. performance (output voltage, capacity, cycling stability, and rate performance) of org. electrode materials in various metal-ion batteries.  The key challenges of org. electrode materials for metal-ion batteries mainly contain the high soly. in electrolyte, low intrinsic electronic cond., large vol. change, and low tap d.  This review provides insights into the development of org. electrode materials with high performance for next-generation rechargeable metal-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrjcOBO_iqopLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lgX3DLpLmziOg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXisFCisrrN&amp;md5=5b60ababd65c10ab8bfcc861dd135386</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref22"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref22'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">22</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit22" data-doi="10.1039/c6cs00173d"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schon, T. Although org. electrode materials for energy storage have progressed in recent years, there are still significant challenges to overcome before reaching large-scale commercialization.  This review provides an overview of energy storage systems as a whole, the metrics that are used to quantify the performance of electrodes, recent strategies that have been investigated to overcome the challenges assocd. with org. electrode materials, and the use of computational chem. to design and study new materials and their properties.         </div><div class="casAbstract">It is a challenge to prep. org. electrodes for sodium-ion batteries with long cycle life and high capacity. Through the resonance effect as well as steric effects, the excessive reactivity of the unpaired electron is successfully suppressed, thus developing an electrode with stable cycling for over 2,000 cycles with 96.8% capacity retention. Here, a facile self-templated strategy is developed to synthesize uniform P2-Na0.7CoO2 microspheres.  Due to the unique microsphere structure, the contact area of the active material with electrolyte is minimized.  As expected, the P2-Na0.7CoO2 microspheres exhibit enhanced electrochem. performance for Na storage in terms of high reversible capacity (125 mAh/g at 5 mA/g), superior rate capability and long cycle life (86% capacity retention over 300 cycles).  Importantly, the synthesis method can be easily extended to synthesize other layered metal oxide (P2-Na0.7MnO2 and O3-NaFeO2) microspheres.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp0tG5Vn0j0XLVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lja8NC0G7lisA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Structural Insight into the Abnormal Capacity of a Co-Substituted Tunnel-Type Na0.44MnO2 Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhong, Wentao; Huang, Qianhui; Zheng, Fenghua; Deng, Qiang; Pan, Qichang; Liu, Yanzhen; Li, Youpeng; Li, Yijuan; Hu, Junhua; Yang, Chenghao; Liu, Meilin</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2020</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">12</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">42</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">47548-47555</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Tunnel-type (T-type) Na0.44MnO2 (NMO) is a promising cathode material for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its high rate performance and cycling stability compared to manganese-based layered oxides.  However, the low specific capacity still restricts its practical applications.  Herein, a Co-doped T-type NMO is synthesized through a facile solid-state reaction method and utilized as a cathode material for SIBs.  A T-type Na0.44Mn0.9925Co0.0075O2 (NMO-3) electrode can deliver a high reversible capacity of 138 mAh g-1 at 0.1C, a superior rate capability (133, 130, 121, 106, and 93 mAh g-1 at 0.5, 1, 2, 5, and 10 C, resp.), and excellent cycling stability (85.2% at 10 C after 500 cycles).  The substitution of Co3+ by Mn3+ leads to the enlargement of small and S-shaped tunnel spaces, which facilitates the insertion/deinsertion of Na+ into/from NMO-3 and greatly enhances its rate capability and cycling stability.  Moreover, the reduced energy barriers for Na+ diffusion in small tunnels make the inactive Na+ easier to be deintercalated, which should be responsible for its high specific capacity that exceeds the theor. capacity of T-type NMO.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGq_JvBuIhvOTrVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lja8NC0G7lisA"> &gt;&gt;         (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">3</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">P2-type Na2/3Fe2/3Mn1/3O2 samples are synthesized by solid-state calcination with different conditions and the influence of synthesis conditions on the structural and electrochem. properties is systematically studied.  By controlling the synthesis conditions, a fraction of O3-type impurity phase is effectively decreased, and nearly stoichiometric P2 Na2/3Fe2/3Mn1/3O2 is successfully obtained by a two-step calcination method.  A voltage plateau of 2.5 V, which is attributed to the oxidn. of Mn3+ to Mn4+, appears in initial charge profiles for quenched and one-step calcined samples.  In contrast, for the initial charge process, the voltage plateau of 2.5 V is not obsd. in the sample prepd. in the two-step calcination process, suggesting that Mn3+ is not contained in this sample.  Charge/discharge mechanisms of nearly stoichiometric Na2/3Fe2/3Mn1/3O2 are also examd. by X-ray absorption spectroscopy and X-ray diffractometry, and it is found that reversible redox reaction of Fe3+/Fe4+ and Mn3+/Mn4+ proceeds on electrochem. cycles.  Moreover, stacking faults assocd. with metal layer glide on charge are more pronounced for P2 Na2/3Fe2/3Mn1/3O2 in comparison to the P2-type Mn-rich system, Na2/3Fe1/2Mn1/2O2.  From these results, factors affecting electrode performance of sodium insertion materials are discussed.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqABh2goIYjKbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lja8NC0G7lisA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1MXos1yitbY%253D&amp;md5=8bc144e28766890209604001bb9bc0f2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref30"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref30'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">30</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit30" data-doi="10.1002/adma.202108304"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wei, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zheng, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chen, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Peng, D.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Ultrahigh-Power Mesocarbon Microbeads|Na + -Diglyme|Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub> )<sub>3</sub> Sodium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit30R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">30</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An Ultrahigh-Power Mesocarbon Microbeads|Na+-Diglyme|Na3V2(PO4)3 Sodium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wei, Qiulong; Chang, Xiaoqing; Wang, Jian; Huang, Tingyi; Huang, Xiaojuan; Yu, Jiayu; Zheng, Hongfei; Chen, Jin-hui; Peng, Dong-Liang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Materials (Weinheim, Germany)</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">34</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2108304</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ADVMEW</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0935-9648</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) show practical applications in large-scale energy storage systems.  But, their power d. is limited by the sluggish Na+ diffusion into the cathode and anode materials.  Herein, the authors demonstrate a prototype of ultrahigh power SIB, consisting of the high-rate Na3V2(PO4)3 (NVP) cathode, graphite-type mesocarbon microbeads (MCMB) anode, and Na+-diglyme electrolyte.  It is found that the overpotential of the NVP cathode obeys the Ohmic rule.  Thus, the as-synthesized NVP@C@carbon nanotubes (CNTs) cathode with the high conductive CNTs networks displays high electronic cond., reducing the overpotential and charge transfer resistances and leading to the remarkable rate capability over 1000C.  For the MCMB anode, the initial [Na-diglyme]+ co-intercalation step is pseudocapacitive dominated, and then the expanded graphite's layers ensure the subsequent fast ions diffusion.  The rapid (de)intercalation kinetics in between the cathode and anode are well-matched.  Thus, the assembled MCMB|1 M NaPF6 in diglyme|NVP@C@CNTs full-cell SIB delivers the energy d. of 88 Wh kg-1 at the high power d. of ∼10 kW kg-1.  Even at the ultrahigh power d. of 23 kW kg-1, an energy d. of 58 Wh kg-1 is obtained.  The encouraging results of the full cell will promote the development of high-power SIB for large-scale applications in the future.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoiycqNbs58GbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lja8NC0G7lisA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit31R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">31</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D graphene decorated Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) microspheres as low-cost and high-performance cathode materials for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yuan, Tianci; Wang, Yanxia; Zhang, Jiexin; Pu, Xiangjun; Ai, Xinping; Chen, Zhongxue; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">56</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">160-168</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion battery has emerged as one of most promising technologies for large-scale energy storage system, and hence has stimulated extensive exploration of applicable electrode materials with low cost and superb electrochem. properties.  Herein, 3D graphene decorated Na4Fe3(PO4)2(P2O7) microspheres as a low-cost and environmentally friendly cathode material are synthesized by using a facile spray-drying method.  The as-prepd. NFPP@rGO composite exhibits a high reversible capacity of 128 mAh g-1 at 0.1 C, a superior rate capability (35 mAh g-1 at 200 C), and a long cycling life (62.3% capacity retention over 6000 cycles at 10 C).  The excellent electrochem. performance is attributed to combined advantages of graphene coating on the surface of nanoparticles and the flexible 3D graphene network, which not only improve the electronic cond., but also accommodate the structural stress of the material during charging and discharging.  Therefore, the NFPP@rGO microsphere with superior electrochem. performances, low-cost raw materials, simple synthetic route and high thermal stability is considered as a very attractive cathode electrode for sodium ion battery.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpOknamjWTFgbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lja8NC0G7lisA"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitlKjsLvO&amp;md5=ded34df0726eab657cccc2c2be06e5e7</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref32"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref32'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">32</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit32" data-doi="10.1038/s41560-017-0014-y"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hong, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lopez, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Feng, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lim, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Chueh, W.                         cas_cit32R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">32</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-performance sodium-organic battery by realizing four-sodium storage in disodium rhodizonate</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Minah; Hong, Jihyun; Lopez, Jeffrey; Sun, Yongming; Feng, Dawei; Lim, Kipil; Chueh, William C.; Toney, Michael F.; Cui, Yi; Bao, Zhenan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">2</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">11</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">861-868</span>CODEN:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) for grid-scale applications need active materials that combine a high energy d. with sustainability.  Given the high theor. specific capacity 501 mAh g-1, and Earth abundance of disodium rhodizonate (Na2C6O6), it is one of the most promising cathodes for SIBs.  However, substantially lower reversible capacities have been obtained compared with the theor. value and the understanding of this discrepancy has been limited.  Here, we reveal that irreversible phase transformation of Na2C6O6 during cycling is the origin of the deteriorating redox activity of Na2C6O6.  The active-particle size and electrolyte conditions were identified as key factors to decrease the activation barrier of the phase transformation during desodiation.  On the basis of this understanding, we achieved four-sodium storage in a Na2C6O6 electrode with a reversible capacity of 484 mAh g-1, an energy d. of 726 Wh kg-1cathode, an energy efficiency above 87% and a good cycle retention.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoauWJJosnmL7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liEWxeyIG2THw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC1cXitVehu78%253D&amp;md5=c2538a0394fd8a1b89f4465c052003f5</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref33'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit33" data-doi="10.1002/adfm.202006066"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shen, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Roy, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances and Optimization Strategies on the Electrolytes for Hard Carbon and P-Based Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Adv.                         cas_cit33R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">33</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Recent Advances and Optimization Strategies on the Electrolytes for Hard Carbon and P-Based Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shen, Liying; Shi, Shanshan; Roy, Swagata; Yin, Xiuping; Liu, Wenbo; Zhao, Yufeng</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Hard carbons (HCs) and P-based materials (including red phosphorus, black phosphorus, and metal phosphides) represent the most promising anodes for the commercialization of sodium ion batteries.  The electrochem. performance of SIBs is detd. not only by the structure of electrode materials, but it is also highly dependent on the matched electrolyte.  In this review, the optimization, the matching strategies and the advanced characterization techniques of the electrolytes system for HCs and P-based anodes are discussed based on the recent advance.  The effective optimization strategies are summarized from three aspects: sodium salts, solvents, and additives.  The challenges and perspectives are also discussed in this review.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGp0OsNcPFxRN7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0liEWxeyIG2THw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXhvFWmsrzJ&amp;md5=df1da94fa44af6ce01dd619317ee762b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.9b01972"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kamiyama, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kubota, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nakano, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fujimura, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shiraishi, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tsukada, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Komaba, S.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">High-Capacity Hard Carbon Synthesized from Macroporous Phenolic Resin for Sodium-Ion and Potassium-Ion Battery</span>. <i>ACS Appl.                         cas_cit34R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">34</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-Capacity Hard Carbon Synthesized from Macroporous Phenolic Resin for Sodium-Ion and Potassium-Ion Battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kamiyama, Azusa; Kubota, Kei; Nakano, Takeshi; Fujimura, Shun; Shiraishi, Soshi; Tsukada, Hidehiko; Komaba, Shinichi</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Hard C is synthesized by heat-treating macroporous phenolic resin at different temps.  The authors study influences of temp. on the structures and electrode properties of the hard C in Na and K cells.  X-ray diffraction and scattering data of the samples confirm the decreased interlayer distance between sp2-C sheets and the expanded internal pores at the raised temps. from 1100 to 1500°.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Extended π-Conjugated System for Fast-Charge and -Discharge Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Chengliang; Xu, Yang; Fang, Yaoguo; Zhou, Min; Liang, Liying; Singh, Sukhdeep; Zhao, Huaping; Schober, Andreas; Lei, Yong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are potential alternatives of current com. inorg. lithium-ion batteries for portable electronics (esp. wearable electronics) because of their low cost and flexibility, making them possible to meet the future flexible and large-scale requirements.  However, only a few org. SIBs have been reported so far, and most of them either were tested in a very slow rate or suffered significant performance degrdn. when cycled under high rate.  Here, we are focusing on the mol. design for improving the battery performance and addressing the current challenge of fast-charge and -discharge.                         cas_cit38R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">38</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Redox Cofactor from Biological Energy Transduction as Molecularly Tunable Energy-Storage Compound</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lee, Minah; Hong, Jihyun; Seo, Dong-Hwa; Nam, Dong Heon; Nam, Ki Tae; Kang, Kisuk; Park, Chan Beum</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2013</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">52</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">32</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">8322-8328</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The possibility is reported of using the energy-storage mechanism of flavin redox cycling in mitochondria to lithium rechargeable batteries.  According to the results, flavin electrodes were capable of reversibly storing and releasing two lithium ions and two electrons per formula unit.  Redox reactions in flavin electrodes were thoroughly investigated using the combined analyses of ex-situ characterizations and d. functional theory (DFT) based calcns.  It is found that the flavin redox reaction occurs during battery operation at the nitrogen atoms of the diazabutadiene motif in flavin mols. using two successive single-electron transfer steps, in a similar way to the proton-coupled electron transfer in flavoenzymes.  Mol. tuning by chem. substitution on the isoalloxazine ring significantly improved electrochem. performances in terms of an av. redox potential, a gravimetric capacity, and stability, resulting in a high-energy d. comparable to that of LiFePO4, the well-known inorg. cathode material for lithium rechargeable batteries.  This work demonstrates a biomimetic approach to design high-performance energy devices based on the analogy between energy-storage phenomena of mitochondria and lithium rechargeable batteries.  It is found that flavins such as vitamin B2 and lumiflavine are capable of reversibly storing lithium by using redox-active nitrogen atoms in the diazabutadiene motif during battery operation.  Analyses of both ex-situ characterizations and DFT calcns. revealed that electron transfer reactions in the flavin electrode during lithium-coupled electron uptake and donation are analogous to the proton-coupled electron transfer mechanism of flavoenzymes.  Proper chem. modification of flavin mols. can improve battery performances; applying strong, electron-withdrawing substituents at the benzene subnucleus and a simple side chain at the pyrazine subnucleus of the isoalloxazine ring, the energy d. of the flavin cathode (i.e. 510 Whkg-1 for lumiflavine) can compete with that of the com. inorg. electrode material, LiFePO4, while more study is required to have lithiated compds. and to overcome the intrinsic low volumetric d. of the org. materials.  These findings confirm that natural living systems, which have become optimized for energy cycling through evolution, hint at unlimited opportunities to design sustainable materials with a superior performance beyond the conventional electrodes in lithium rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGobchuKR1LZurVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgDCGLanCGlQ"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit39R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">39</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dual Active Site of the Azo and Carbonyl-Modified Covalent Organic Framework for High-Performance Li Storage</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zhao, Genfu; Zhang, Yuhao; Gao, Zhihui; Li, Huani; Liu, Shuming; Cai, Sheng; Yang, Xiaofei; Guo, Hong; Sun, Xueliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Energy Letters</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Org. electrode materials play a crucial role in environmentally friendly and sustainable lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) due to their abundance, high theor. capacity, inexpensiveness, and recyclability.  However, crit. issues such as fewer redox-active sites and poor structural stability limit their extensive application in LIBs.  Herein, a unique covalent org. framework (Tp-Azo-COF) with a dual active site of N=N and C=O is designed and successfully applied as the anode material for LIBs.  Benefiting from its abundance of active sites, large conjugate structure, large surface area, and accessible Li+ transport channels, the Tp-Azo-COF anode materials present high electrochem. kinetics and structural stability.  The assembled LIBs deliver a specific capability of 305.97 mAh g-1 at a c.d. of 1000 mA g-1 after 3000 cycles.  This work may inspire avenues for the development of advanced org. materials of inexpensive, sustainable, and durable rechargeable batteries.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGr4g689Q9AD1bVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljgDCGLanCGlQ"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BB3cXksVyjtb4%253D&amp;md5=14cc30aab4b2c011dcf7f9d769dcff8f</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref40'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/am5060959"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Häupler, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hagemann, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Friebe, C.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wild, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Schubert, U.                         cas_cit40R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">40</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Dithiophenedione-containing polymers for battery application</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Haupler Bernhard; Hagemann Tino; Friebe Christian; Wild Andreas; Schubert Ulrich S</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS applied materials &amp; interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">7</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3473-9</span>
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn"></span>.
    </div><div class="casAbstract">Redox-active polymers have received recently significant interest as active materials in secondary organic batteries.  We designed a redox-active monomer, namely 2-vinyl-4,8-dihydrobenzo[1,2-b:4,5-b']dithiophene-4,8-dione that exhibits two one-electron redox reactions and has a low molar mass, resulting in a high theoretical capacity of 217 mAh/g.  The free radical polymerization of the monomer was optimized by variation of solvent and initiator.  The electrochemical behavior of the obtained polymer was investigated using cyclic voltammetry.  The utilization of lithium salts in the supporting electrolyte leads to a merging of the redox waves accompanied by a shift to higher redox potentials.  Prototype batteries manufactured with 10 wt % polymer as active material exhibit full material activity at the first charge/discharge cycle.  During the first 100 cycles, the capacity drops to 50%.  Higher contents of polymer (up to 40 wt %) leads to a lower material activity.  Furthermore, the battery system reveals a fast charge/discharge ability, allowing a maximum speed up to 10C (6 min) with only a negligible loss of capacity.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=LOZGTtr2ZcQgWmaUaiYKy5ZoeNcnHOQ9fW6udTcc2eZEOiBoND2cpLntkvexoksv"> &gt;&gt; Soc.</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2019</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>141</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">9623</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">9628</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/jacs.9b03467</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D141%26publication_year%3D2019%26pages%3D9623-9628%26journal%3DJ.%2BAm.%2BChem.%2BSoc.%26author%3DS.%2BGu%26author%3DS.%2BWu%26author%3DL.%2BCao%26author%3DM.%2BLi%26author%3DN.%2BQin%26author%3DJ.%2BZhu%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DY.%2BLi%26author%3DZ.%2BLi%26author%3DJ.%2BChen%26author%3DZ.%2BLu%26title%3DTunable%2BRedox%2BChemistry%2Band%2BStability%2Bof%2BRadical%2BIntermediates%2Bin%2B2D%2BCovalent%2BOrganic%2BFrameworks%2Bfor%2BHigh%2BPerformance%2BSodium%2BIon%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1021%252Fjacs.9b03467&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c07383&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Fjacs.9b03467&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit41R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">41</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Tunable Redox Chemistry and Stability of Radical Intermediates in 2D Covalent Organic Frameworks for High Performance Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Gu, Shuai; Wu, Shaofei; Cao, Lujie; Li, Minchan; Qin, Ning; Zhu, Jian; Wang, Zhiqiang; Li, Yingzhi; Li, Zhiqiang; Chen, Jingjing; Lu, Zhouguang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of the American Chemical Society</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2019</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">141</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">24</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9623-9628</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JACSAT</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0002-7863</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Radicals are inevitable intermediates during the charging and discharging of org. redox electrodes.  The increase of the reactivity of the radical intermediates is desirable to maximize the capacity and enhance the rate capability but is detrimental to cycling stability.  Therefore, it is a great challenge to controllably balance the redox reactivity and stability of radical intermediates to optimize the electrochem. properties with a good combination of high specific capacity, excellent rate capability, and long-term cycle life.  Herein, we reported the redox and tunable stability of radical intermediates in covalent org. frameworks (COFs) considered as high capacity and stable anode for sodium-ion batteries.  The comprehensive characterizations combined with theor. simulation confirmed that the redox of C-O· and α-C radical intermediates play an important role in the sodiation/desodiation process.  Specifically, the stacking behavior could be feasibly tuned by the thickness of 2D COFs, essentially detg. the redox reactivity and stability of the α-C radical intermediates and their contributive capacity.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The carboxylate group-based org. electrode materials are promising anodes for rechargeable sodium ion batteries (SIBs) due to the low cost, abundance, environmental benignity and high sustainability of org. materials.  Here, we compare the electrochem. performance of three carboxylate group-based org. electrode materials in SIBs, and identify that the two carboxylate groups in the para position of the benzene ring are electrochem. active centers to reversibly react with Na-ions and electrons.  The carboxylate group-based anode, trisodium 1,2,4-benzenetricarboxylate (TBC), exhibits exceptional electrochem. performance in SIBs, in terms of high specific capacity (195 mAh g-1) and long cycle life (600 cycles).  The third carboxylate group in TBC enhances the sodiation/de-sodiation potentials, and reduces its soly. in the electrolyte, resulting in a highly stable org. anode.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Infrared and Raman spectroscopic study of carboxylic acids in heavy water</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Genin, Francine; Quiles, Fabienne; Burneau, Andre</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Physical Chemistry Chemical Physics</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">IR and Raman spectra of CH3COOD (I) and CD3COOD (II) were obtained below 1900 cm-1, from dil. solns. in heavy water up to neat liqs.  The relation of the intermol. interactions with the acid concn. is discussed.  In the debate concerning the structure of pure liq. acetic acid at room temp., we favor the assignment of the major species to the centrosym. dimer.  This is based not only on the literature data for crystal, liq. and vapor acetic acid, but also on the IR and Raman spectra of liq. acetic and propanoic acids and their 0.1 M solns. in water.  On increasing the acid concn. from dil. solns., the hydrated monomer is progressively replaced by more or less hydrated linear dimer and then by the cyclic dimer.  At a molar fraction of 0.5, the three kinds of species coexist.  At still higher concns., longer oligomers appear while the cyclic dimer dominates the other species.  A comprehensive assignment of the IR and Raman spectra is given on the basis of a previously published ab initio calcn. for monomer, cyclic and linear dimers.  A narrow well resolved satellite band is obsd. for the hydrated monomer some 45 cm-1 above the CC bond stretching vibration (νCC), not only for I and II but also for C2H5COOD and CH2ClCOOD, specifically in dil. heavy water solns.  It is not easily assigned to overtones or combination bands simultaneously for the three mols.  Both a blue-shift and a narrowing of the νCC band are usually obsd. by ionization of a carboxylic acid into a carboxylate ion in water.                         cas_cit45R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">45</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Characterization of Conformation and Locations of C-F Bonds in Graphene Derivative by Polarized ATR-FTIR</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Xu; Wang, Weimiao; Liu, Yang; Ren, Mengmeng; Xiao, Huining; Liu, Xiangyang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Analytical Chemistry (Washington, DC, United States)</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">It is still a challenge to explore the orientation and location of chem. groups in the two-dimensional deriv. of graphene.  In this study, polarized attenuated total reflectance Fourier transform IR spectroscopy (polarized ATR-FTIR) was employed to investigate the orientation and location of C-F groups in the corresponding graphene deriv. sheets, which facilitates building a relationship between the bonding nature and fine structure.  There were two types of C-F bonding, (C-F)I and (C-F)II, in fluorinated graphene sheets.  It was found that (C-F)II bonds were linked at the coplanar carbon atoms in the weakly fluorinated region (CxF, x ≥ 2), whereas the (C-F)I bonds cluster at the strongly deformed carbon framework with a F/C ratio of about 1.  The thermostability of (C-F)II is lower than that of (C-F)I bonds.  This is because the coplanar structure of the weakly fluorinated region tends to transform to the planar arom. ring with the breaking of the C-F bond as compared with the strong fluorinated nonplanar region.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGoGyZFGrsRv7LVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhc9g6I5QsGGg"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XjvFyrt70%253D&amp;md5=cd3f10d0e97efdf6b5e762614109ee3c</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref46"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref46'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">46</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit46" data-doi="10.3390/molecules18066829"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nagels, N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hauchecorne, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Herrebout, W.     <span class="NLM_cas:volume">18</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The formation of halogen bonded complexes formed between the trifluorohalomethanes CF3Cl, CF3Br and CF3I and the Lewis bases benzene and toluene at temps. below 150K was investigated using FTIR and Raman spectroscopy.  Expts. using liq. krypton as solvent show that for both CF3Br and CF3I substantial fractions of the monomers can be involved in 1:1 complexes.  In addn., weak absorptions illustrating the formation of 2:1 complexes between CF3I and benzene are obsd.  Using spectra recorded at temps. between 120 and 140 K, obsd. information on the relative stability was obtained for all complexes by detg. the complexation enthalpies in soln.                         cas_cit49R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">49</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">High-rate electrochemical energy storage through Li+ intercalation pseudocapacitance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Augustyn, Veronica; Come, Jeremy; Lowe, Michael A.; Kim, Jong Woung; Taberna, Pierre-Louis; Tolbert, Sarah H.; Abruna, Hector D.; Simon, Patrice; Dunn, Bruce</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Pseudocapacitance is commonly assocd. with surface or near-surface reversible redox reactions, as obsd. with RuO2·xH2O in an acidic electrolyte.  However, we recently demonstrated that a pseudocapacitive mechanism occurs when lithium ions are inserted into mesoporous and nanocrystal films of orthorhombic Nb2O5 (T-Nb2O5; refs , ).  Here, we quantify the kinetics of charge storage in T-Nb2O5: currents that vary inversely with time, charge-storage capacity that is mostly independent of rate, and redox peaks that exhibit small voltage offsets even at high rates.  We also define the structural characteristics necessary for this process, termed intercalation pseudocapacitance, which are a cryst. network that offers two-dimensional transport pathways and little structural change on intercalation.  The principal benefit realized from intercalation pseudocapacitance is that high levels of charge storage are achieved within short periods of time because there are no limitations from solid-state diffusion.  Thick electrodes (up to 40 μm thick) prepd. with T-Nb2O5 offer the promise of exploiting intercalation pseudocapacitance to obtain high-rate charge-storage devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder ®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGrPatnkXnvsNbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0ljEAxpiXIvxSA"> &gt;&gt;                         cas_cit50R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">50</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Reversible multi-electron redox chemistry of π-conjugated N-containing heteroaromatic molecule-based organic cathodes</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Peng, Chengxin; Ning, Guo-Hong; Su, Jie; Zhong, Guiming; Tang, Wei; Tian, Bingbing; Su, Chenliang; Yu, Dingyi; Zu, Lianhai; Yang, Jinhu; Ng, Man-Fai; Hu, Yong-Sheng; Yang, Yong; Armand, Michel; Loh, Kian Ping</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nature Energy</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Even though org. mols. with well-designed functional groups can be programmed to have high electron d. per unit mass, their poor elec. cond. and low cycle stability limit their applications in batteries.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Defective Hard Carbon Anode for Na-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Zhifei; Chen, Yicong; Jian, Zelang; Jiang, Heng; Razink, Joshua James; Stickle, William F.; Neuefeind, Joerg C.; Ji, Xiulei</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">30</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">14</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">4536-4542</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">CMATEX</span>;
